The main candidates for the <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_presidential_election,_2005" title="Sri Lankan presidential election, 2005">election</a>, which was held in November, were UNF candidate former Prime Minister Ranil Wickremasinghe, who advocated the reopening of talks with the LTTE, and the UPFA candidate Prime Minister Rajapaksa, who called for a tougher line against the LTTE and a renegotiation of the cease-fire. The LTTE openly called for a <a href="/wiki/Boycott" title="Boycott">boycott</a> of the election by Tamils. Many of them were expected to vote for Wickremasinghe, and the loss of their votes proved fatal to his chances, as Rajapakse achieved a narrow victory. Following the election, LTTE leader <a href="/wiki/Velupillai_Prabhakaran" title="Velupillai Prabhakaran">Velupillai Prabhakaran</a> stated in his annual address that the Tigers would "renew their struggle" in 2006 if the government did not take serious moves toward peace.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Resumption_of_hostilities">Resumption of hostilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Resumption of hostilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Extent_of_territorial_control_in_sri_lanka.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="601" height="351" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Extent_of_territorial_control_in_sri_lanka.png/220px-Extent_of_territorial_control_in_sri_lanka.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Extent_of_territorial_control_in_sri_lanka.png/330px-Extent_of_territorial_control_in_sri_lanka.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Extent_of_territorial_control_in_sri_lanka.png/440px-Extent_of_territorial_control_in_sri_lanka.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Extent_of_territorial_control_in_sri_lanka.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Red area shows the approximate areas of Sri Lanka controlled by the LTTE and the Government, as of December 2005.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Eelam_War_IV" title="Eelam War IV">Eelam War IV</a></div>
<p>Beginning in December 2005, there was increased guerrilla activity to the northeast, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M18A1_Claymore_Antipersonnel_Mine" title="M18A1 Claymore Antipersonnel Mine">Claymore mine</a> attacks which killed 150 government troops,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-st1_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-st1-95">[95]</a></sup> clashes between the <a href="/wiki/Sea_Tigers" title="Sea Tigers">Sea Tigers</a> and the Sri Lanka navy and the killings of sympathizers on both sides including <a href="/wiki/Taraki_Sivaram" title="Taraki Sivaram">Taraki Sivaram</a>, a pro-LTTE journalist, and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Pararajasingham" title="Joseph Pararajasingham">Joseph Pararajasingham</a>, a pro-LTTE MP, both killed allegedly by the government of Sri Lanka.</p>
<p>At the beginning of 2006 the focus of the civil war turned to civilian targets, with commuter bus and train bombings carried out in most parts of the country, including a series of attacks against commuters in and around Colombo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Talks_and_further_violence">Talks and further violence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Talks and further violence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In light of this violence, the co-chairs of the Tokyo Donor conference called on both parties to return to the negotiating table. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_State_Department" title="US State Department">US State Department</a> officials gave warnings to the Tigers, stating that a return to hostilities would mean that the Tigers would face a "more capable and more determined" Sri Lankan military.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ind1_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-ind1-97">[97]</a></sup> While the talks were going on there was violence directed towards civilians, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2006_Trincomalee_massacre" title="2006 Trincomalee massacre">the killings of five Tamil students</a> on 2 January 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a last-minute effort to salvage an agreement between the parties, Norwegian special envoy <a href="/wiki/Erik_Solheim" title="Erik Solheim">Erik Solheim</a> and LTTE theoretician Anton Balasingham arrived on the island. The parties strongly disagreed on the location of the talks; however, continued efforts produced a breakthrough when both parties agreed on 7 February 2006 that new talks could be held in <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a>, Switzerland, on 22 and 23 February. During the weeks after the talks there was a significant decrease in violence. However, the LTTE resumed attacks against the military in April.</p>
<p>In light of this violence, the LTTE called for a postponement of the Geneva talks until 24–25 April, and the government initially agreed to this. Following negotiations, both the government and the rebels agreed to have a civilian vessel transport regional LTTE leaders with international truce monitors on 16 April, which involved crossing government-controlled territory. However, the climate shifted drastically when the Tigers cancelled the meeting, claiming not to have agreed to a naval escort. According to the SLMM, the Tamil rebels had previously agreed to the escort.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc8_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc8-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 20 April 2006 the LTTE officially pulled out of peace talks indefinitely. While they stated that transportation issues had prevented them from meeting their regional leaders, some analysts and the international community were strongly skeptical, seeing the transportation issue as a delaying tactic by the LTTE to avoid attending peace talks in Geneva.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc9_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc9-101">[101]</a></sup> Violence continued to spiral and on 23 April 2006, <a href="/wiki/Gomarankadawala_massacre" title="Gomarankadawala massacre">six Sinhalese rice farmers were massacred</a> in their paddy fields by suspected LTTE cadres,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> and on 13 May 2006 <a href="/wiki/Allaipiddy_massacre" title="Allaipiddy massacre">13 Tamil civilians were killed</a> in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Sri_Lanka#Northern_Province" title="List of islands of Sri Lanka">islet of Kayts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> International condemnation against the LTTE skyrocketed following the attempted assassination of the commander of the Sri Lanka Army, Lt. Gen. <a href="/wiki/Sarath_Fonseka" title="Sarath Fonseka">Sarath Fonseka</a>, by a female LTTE <a href="/wiki/Black_Tigers" title="Black Tigers">Black Tiger</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suicide_bomber" title="Suicide bomber">suicide bomber</a> named Anoja Kugenthirasah, who concealed the explosives by appearing to be pregnant and blew herself up at army headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Colombo" title="Colombo">Colombo</a>. For the first time since the 2001 cease-fire, the Sri Lanka Air Force carried out aerial assaults on rebel positions in the northeastern part of the island in retaliation for the attack.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>This attack, along with the assassination of Lakshman Kadiragamar a year earlier and an unsuccessful attack against a naval vessel carrying 710 unarmed security force personnel on holiday, marked a turning point, as the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> decided to proscribe the LTTE as a terrorist organisation on 19 May 2006. It resulted in the freezing of LTTE assets in its 27 member nations. In a statement, the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> said that the LTTE did not represent all the Tamils and called on it to "allow for political pluralism and alternate democratic voices in the northern and eastern parts of Sri Lanka".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hindu1_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-hindu1-105">[105]</a></sup> As the north and east of the country continued to be rocked by attacks, new talks were scheduled in Oslo, Norway, between 8–9 June. Delegations from both sides arrived in Oslo, but the talks were cancelled when the LTTE refused to meet directly with the government delegation, claiming its fighters were not allowed safe passage to travel to the talks. Norwegian mediator Erik Solheim told journalists that the LTTE should take direct responsibility for the collapse of the talks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc10_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc10-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>Further violence followed, including the <a href="/wiki/Vankalai_massacre" title="Vankalai massacre">Vankalai massacre</a>. The Sri Lankan army and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tamil_Tiger" title="Tamil Tiger">Tamil Tiger</a> rebels blamed each other for the killings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AN_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-AN-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> There was also the <a href="/wiki/Kebithigollewa_massacre" title="Kebithigollewa massacre">Kebithigollewa massacre</a> in which the LTTE attacked a bus, killing at least 64 Sinhalese civilians and prompting more air strikes by the Air Force,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usinfo1_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-usinfo1-109">[109]</a></sup> and the assassination of Sri Lanka's third highest-ranking army officer and Deputy Chief of Staff <a href="/wiki/Parami_Kulatunga" title="Parami Kulatunga">General Parami Kulatunga</a> on 26 June by an LTTE suicide bomber.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc11_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc11-110">[110]</a></sup> These events led the <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Monitoring_Mission" title="Sri Lanka Monitoring Mission">SLMM</a> to question whether a cease-fire could still be said to exist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slmm1_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-slmm1-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mavil_Aru_water_dispute">Mavil Aru water dispute</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Mavil Aru water dispute">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A new crisis leading to the first large-scale fighting since signing of the cease-fire occurred when the LTTE closed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sluice_gate" title="Sluice gate">sluice gates</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Mavil_Aru" title="Mavil Aru">Mavil Aru</a> reservoir on 21 July. Mavil Aru was the waterway that provided water to some regions of eastern Sri Lanka, like <a href="/wiki/Trincomalee" title="Trincomalee">Trincomalee</a>. After the cease-fire in 2002, the conflict over Mavil Aru was one of the biggest military confrontations between the <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Armed_Forces" title="Sri Lanka Armed Forces">Sri Lanka Armed Forces</a> and the LTTE. Its relevance is for geo-strategic reasons: within the Mavil Aru area, Sinhala, Muslim and Tamil populations live side by side. It is also the entrance to Koddiyar Bay, the inlet for Trincomalee port and naval base, so the LTTE presence in the area seriously threatened the Sri Lankan security forices' presence and domination.</p>
<p>Closure of Mavil Aru affected the water supply to 15,000 families in government-controlled areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc12_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc12-112">[112]</a></sup> After the initial negotiations and efforts by the SLMM to open the gates failed, the Sri Lanka military initiated an operation to achieve the re-opening of the sluice gates.</p>
<p>President Rajapaksa said that the supply of water was a non-negotiable fundamental human right. Additionally, a government spokesman said that "<i>utilities could not be used as bargaining tools</i>" by the rebels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc12_112-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbc12-112">[112]</a></sup> The government deployed its army and air force for the offensive, attacking not only the region of <a href="/wiki/Mavil_Aru" title="Mavil Aru">Mavil Aru</a> but also the LTTE positions in <a href="/wiki/Batticaloa" title="Batticaloa">Batticaloa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vavuniya" title="Vavuniya">Vavuniya</a>. Air Force planes attacked LTTE positions on 26 July, and ground troops began an operation to open the gate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-south_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-south-113">[113]</a></sup> The sluice gates were eventually reopened on 8 August, with conflicting reports as to who actually opened them. Initially, the SLMM claimed that they managed to persuade the LTTE to lift the waterway blockade conditionally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nation.lk_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-nation.lk-114">[114]</a></sup> The LTTE claimed that it opened the sluice gates "on humanitarian grounds", although this was disputed by military correspondents, who stated the water began flowing immediately after security forces carried out a precise bombing of the Mavil Aru anicut.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-st2_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-st2-115">[115]</a></sup> Eventually, following heavy fighting, government troops gained full control of the Mavil Aru reservoir on 15 August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nation.lk_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-nation.lk-114">[114]</a></sup> The consequences of the "Operation Watershed" were about 150 civilians killed and more than 50,000 refugees from <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mutur&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mutur (page does not exist)">Mutur</a> and the villages nearby. It was the precedent of the <a href="/wiki/Eelam_War_IV" title="Eelam War IV">Eelam War IV</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-south_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-south-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="LTTE_offensives_in_Muttur_and_Jaffna">LTTE offensives in Muttur and Jaffna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: LTTE offensives in Muttur and Jaffna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As fierce fighting was ongoing in the vicinity of Mavil Aru, violence spread to Trincomalee, where the LTTE launched an attack on a crucial Sri Lanka Navy base,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-south2_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-south2-116">[116]</a></sup> and to the strategic government-controlled coastal town of Muttur in early August, resulting in the deaths of at least 30 civilians and displacing 25,000 residents of the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> The clashes erupted on 2 August 2006 when the LTTE launched a heavy artillery attack on Muttur<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toi1_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-toi1-118">[118]</a></sup> and then moved in, gaining control of some parts of the town.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hindu2_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-hindu2-119">[119]</a></sup> The military retaliated, and re-established full control over the town by 5 August, killing over 150 LTTE fighters in heavy clashes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toi1_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-toi1-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>Soon afterwards, 17 persons working for the International French charity <a href="/wiki/Action_Against_Hunger" title="Action Against Hunger">Action Against Hunger</a> (ACF) in Muthur, <a href="/wiki/2006_Trincomalee_massacre_of_NGO_workers" title="2006 Trincomalee massacre of NGO workers">were massacred</a>. They were found lying face down on the floor of their office, shot to death, still wearing their clearly marked T-shirts indicating they were international humanitarian workers. The murders prompted widespread international condemnation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> The SLMM claimed that the government was behind the attack,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> but the government denied the allegation calling it "pathetic and biased", and stated that the SLMM had "no right to make such a statement because they are not professionals in autopsy or post-mortem."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>Meanwhile, in the north of the country, some of the bloodiest fighting since 2001 took place after the LTTE launched massive attacks on <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Army" title="Sri Lanka Army">Sri Lanka Army</a> defense lines on the Jaffna peninsula on 11 August. The LTTE used a force of 400-500 fighters in the attacks, which consisted of land and amphibious assaults, and also fired a barrage of artillery at government positions, including the key military airbase at <a href="/wiki/Palaly_Military_Base" title="Palaly Military Base">Palaly</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-south2_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-south2-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oi1_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-oi1-123">[123]</a></sup> The LTTE is estimated to have lost over 200 fighters in the operation, while 90 Sri Lankan soldiers and sailors were also killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usatoday1_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday1-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<p>As ground battles were ongoing in the north and the east of the country, the Sri Lanka Air Force carried out an air strike against a facility in the rebel-held Mullaitivu area, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chencholai_airstrike" title="Chencholai airstrike">killing a number of Tamil girls</a>. Although the LTTE claimed 61 girls were killed, the SLMM stated they were able to count just 19 bodies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hind_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-hind-125">[125]</a></sup> The government stated that it was an LTTE training facility and that the children were LTTE child soldiers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> although the LTTE claimed the victims were schoolgirls attending a course on first aid at an orphanage.</p>
<p>On the same day a convoy carrying the Pakistani <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_Commissioner" title="High Commissioner">High Commissioner</a> to Sri Lanka, Bashir Wali Mohamed, was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pakistani_ambassador_to_Sri_lanka" title="Attack on Pakistani ambassador to Sri lanka">attacked</a> when a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M18A1_Claymore_Antipersonnel_Mine" title="M18A1 Claymore Antipersonnel Mine">claymore antipersonnel mine</a> concealed within an <a href="/wiki/Auto_rickshaw" title="Auto rickshaw">auto rickshaw</a> blew up as it passed by. The High Commissioner escaped unhurt, but seven people were killed and 17 injured in the blast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc4789991_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc4789991-127">[127]</a></sup> The High Commissioner claimed that India was believed to have carried it out,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-at2_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-at2-128">[128]</a></sup> in order to intimidate Pakistan, which is one of the main suppliers of military equipment to the Sri Lankan government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-at2_128-1"><a href="#cite_note-at2-128">[128]</a></sup> Pakistan had promised one shipload of equipment every 10 days in coming months.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fall_of_Sampur">Fall of Sampur</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Fall of Sampur">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since the resumption of violence, concerns were mounting among the military establishment that the strategically crucial<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters1_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters1-129">[129]</a></sup> Sri Lanka Navy base in Trincomalee was under severe threat from LTTE gun positions located in and around Sampur, which lies across the Koddiyar Bay from Trincomalee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hindu4_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-hindu4-130">[130]</a></sup> Artillery fired from LTTE bases in the area could potentially cripple the naval base, bringing it to a complete standstill and cutting the only military supply chain to Jaffna. All movements of naval vessels were also under the constant surveillance of the LTTE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-south3_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-south3-131">[131]</a></sup> These fears were backed up by a US military advisory team which visited the island in 2005.</p>
<p>Following clashes in Mavil Aru and Muttur, the LTTE had intensified attacks targeting the naval base in Trincomalee,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hindu4_130-1"><a href="#cite_note-hindu4-130">[130]</a></sup> and in a speech on 21 August Sri Lankan president Mahinda Rajapakse made clear the government intentions were to neutralize the LTTE threat from Sampur.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hindu4_130-2"><a href="#cite_note-hindu4-130">[130]</a></sup> On 28 August the military launched an assault to retake the LTTE camps in Sampur and the adjoining Kaddaiparichchan and Thoppur areas. This led the LTTE to declare that if the offensive continued, the cease-fire would be officially over.</p>
<p>After steady progress, security forces led by Brigade Commander Sarath Wijesinghe<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hindu5_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-hindu5-132">[132]</a></sup> recaptured Sampur from the LTTE on 4 September and began to establish military bases there,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> as the LTTE admitted defeat and stated their fighters "withdrew" from the strategically important town.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> It marked the first significant territorial change of hands since the signing of the cease-fire agreement in 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iht1_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-iht1-135">[135]</a></sup> The Sri Lankan military estimated that 33 of its personnel were killed in the offensive, along with over 200 LTTE fighters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hindu5_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-hindu5-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="LTTE_retaliation_and_further_peace_talks">LTTE retaliation and further peace talks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: LTTE retaliation and further peace talks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The LTTE struck back in October. First, they killed nearly 130 soldiers in a fierce battle at Muhamalai, the crossing-point between government- and LTTE-controlled area in the north of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sunday1_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-sunday1-136">[136]</a></sup> Just days later, a suspected LTTE suicide bomber <a href="/wiki/2006_Digampathana_bombing" title="2006 Digampathana bombing">struck a naval convoy</a> in Habarana, in the center of the country, killing about 100 sailors who were returning home on leave.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> It was the deadliest suicide attack in the history of the conflict.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zaman1_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-zaman1-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<p>Two days later LTTE Sea Tiger forces launched an attack against the <i>Dakshina</i> naval base in the southern port city of <a href="/wiki/Galle" title="Galle">Galle</a>. It was the farthest south any major LTTE attack had taken place, and involved 15 LTTE fighters who arrived in five suicide boats. The attack was repulsed by the government, and the damage to the naval base was minimal. All 15 LTTE fighers were believed to have died in the attack, along with one Navy sailor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hindu6_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-hindu6-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite these incidents, both parties agreed to unconditionally attend peace talks in Geneva on 28–29 October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-south4_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-south4-140">[140]</a></sup> However, the peace talks broke down due to disagreements over the reopening of the key A9 highway, which is the link between Jaffna and government-controlled areas in the south. While the LTTE wanted the highway, which was closed following fierce battles in August, to be reopened, the government refused, stating the LTTE would use it to collect taxes from people passing through and would use it to launch further offensives against government troops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the dawn of the new year, suspected <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LTTE" title="LTTE">LTTE</a> fighters carried out two bus bombings in the south of the country, killing 21 civilians. News reports stated that the attacks bore all the hallmarks of an LTTE attack.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-an1_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-an1-142">[142]</a></sup> The Sri Lankan government condemned the attacks and blamed the LTTE for carrying them out, although the LTTE denied any involvement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcns1_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-mcns1-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_offensive_in_the_East">Government offensive in the East</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Government offensive in the East">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Theater_of_Eelam_War_IV" title="Eastern Theater of Eelam War IV">Eastern Theater of Eelam War IV</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Operation_Definite_Victory" title="Operation Definite Victory">Operation Definite Victory</a></div>
<p>In December 2006 Sri Lankan government officials announced their plans to drive the LTTE out of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Province,_Sri_Lanka" title="Eastern Province, Sri Lanka">Eastern Province</a> of Sri Lanka, and then use the full strength of the military to defeat the LTTE in the north of the country. The government stated that LTTE was firing artillery towards civilian settlements in the east and were using 35,000 people as human shields.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters-14_December_2006_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-14_December_2006-144">[144]</a></sup> These claims were later backed up by civilians in the area, who told reporters that they were held by force by the Tamil Tigers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iht-18_December_2006_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-iht-18_December_2006-145">[145]</a></sup> On 7 November 2006, amidst conflicting claims, over 45 Tamil civilians were killed in what is known as the <a href="/wiki/Vaharai_bombing" title="Vaharai bombing">Vaharai bombing</a>.</p>
<p>Subsequently, the army began an offensive against the LTTE on 8 December 2006, in the Batticoloa district with the objective of taking <a href="/wiki/Vakarai_(Sri_Lanka)" title="Vakarai (Sri Lanka)">Vakarai</a>, the principal stronghold of the LTTE in the east; the operation was temporarily aborted after a week of fighting due to the large number of civilians in the area and the difficulty in conducting combat operations due to the ongoing <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a> rain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uthr1_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-uthr1-146">[146]</a></sup> Over the next few weeks an estimated 20,000 civilians fled from <a href="/wiki/Vakarai" title="Vakarai">Vakarai</a> to government-controlled areas, fearing the imminent assault. The army launched a new offensive in mid-January, and Vakarai fell to the advancing troops on 19 January. While the offensive in the East was ongoing, the LTTE and others accused the government of murdering 15 civilians in the <a href="/wiki/Padahuthurai_bombing" title="Padahuthurai bombing">Padahuthurai bombing</a> on 2 January, when the air force bombed what they claimed to be an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LTTE" title="LTTE">LTTE</a> naval base in Illuppaikadavai in northern Sri Lanka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trib1_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-trib1-147">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> The loss of Vakarai had been predicted to cut off supply routes of the northern Tigers to their cadres in the east, thus weakening the Tigers' already diminishing grip on the east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>As the military offensive was ongoing, the LTTE continued to carry out attacks against civilians in government-held territory. On 1 April 2007 the military accused the LTTE of killing six Sinhalese tsunami aid workers in the eastern district of Batticaloa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smh-4.2F2.2F07_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-smh-4.2F2.2F07-151">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toi-4.2F2.2F07_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-toi-4.2F2.2F07-152">[152]</a></sup> The next day suspected LTTE fighters set off a bomb aboard a civilian bus in Ampara, which killed 17 people, including three children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc-4.2F2.2F07_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-4.2F2.2F07-153">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-bus-4.2F2.2F07_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-bus-4.2F2.2F07-154">[154]</a></sup></p>
<p>Troops mostly operating in small groups of Special Forces and Commando units began a new operation in February<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ra-4.2F12.2F07_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-ra-4.2F12.2F07-155">[155]</a></sup> to clear the last remaining LTTE fighters from the Eastern Province. As part of the operation, troops captured the key LTTE base in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kokkadicholai" title="Kokkadicholai">Kokkadicholai</a> on 28 March,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-kkd-28_March_2007_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-kkd-28_March_2007-156">[156]</a></sup> and the strategic <a href="/wiki/A5_highway_(Sri_Lanka)" title="A5 highway (Sri Lanka)">A5 highway</a> on 12 April, bringing the entire highway under government control for the first time in 15 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-a5-4.2F12.2F07_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-a5-4.2F12.2F07-157">[157]</a></sup> This meant the LTTE's presence in the rast was reduced to a 140-square-kilometer pocket of jungle in the Thoppigala area northwest of Batticaloa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ra-4.2F12.2F07_155-1"><a href="#cite_note-ra-4.2F12.2F07-155">[155]</a></sup> After the three-month-long <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Thoppigala" title="Battle of Thoppigala">Battle of Thoppigala</a>, the army captured the Thoppigala peak on 11 July 2007, ending the LTTE's military capability in the Eastern Province and concluding Eelam War IV in the Eastern theatre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baron.27s_cap_battle-2007-07-11_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-Baron.27s_cap_battle-2007-07-11-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_offensive_in_the_North">Government offensive in the North</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Government offensive in the North">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%932009_SLA_Northern_offensive" title="2008–2009 SLA Northern offensive">2008–2009 SLA Northern offensive</a></div>
<p>Sporadic fighting in the North had been going on for months, but the intensity of the clashes increased after September 2007. During clashes in the Forward Defence Lines, separating their forces, both sides exchanged heavy artillery fire, after which military incursions followed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> By December 2007, the LTTE defences at Uyilankulama, Parappakandal and Thampanai were lost to advancing troops of the Sri Lanka Army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-ma-22_December_2007_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-ma-22_December_2007-160">[160]</a></sup></p>
<p>In an interview with the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunday_Observer" title="Sunday Observer">Sunday Observer</a></i> the Army Commander Lt. Gen. Sarath Fonseka said that the Army had occupied the LTTE's Forward Defence Lines and surrounded the Wanni LTTE bases from all directions. He also said that there were around 3,000 Tigers remaining and that the military intended to annihilate them within the first six months of the next year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-no-30_December_2007_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-no-30_December_2007-161">[161]</a></sup> A day later there were less optimistic statements by Army, Air Force and Navy Commanders. The Army was to face an estimated 5,000 Tiger cadres in the Wanni. The Commander of the Army intended to shift the current battles in the Forward Defence Lines to a decisive phase in August 2008. In the Commanders' view, it was quite possible to defeat the LTTE in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2b_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2b-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Military of Sri Lanka">military of Sri Lanka</a> claimed that the leader of the LTTE, <a href="/wiki/Velupillai_Prabhakaran" title="Velupillai Prabhakaran">Velupillai Prabhakaran</a>, was seriously injured during air strikes carried out by the <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Air_Force" title="Sri Lanka Air Force">Sri Lanka Air Force</a> on a bunker complex in Jayanthinagar on 26 November 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-vp-19_December_2007_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-vp-19_December_2007-163">[163]</a></sup> Earlier, on 2 November 2007, <a href="/wiki/S._P._Thamilselvan" title="S. P. Thamilselvan">S. P. Thamilselvan</a>, the head of the LTTE political wing, was killed during another government air raid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> The Sri Lanka Air Force openly vowed to destroy the entire leadership of the LTTE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2b_162-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2b-162">[162]</a></sup> On 5 January 2008, Colonel Charles, Head of LTTE Military Intelligence, was killed in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Claymore_mine" title="Claymore mine">claymore mine</a> ambush by a <a href="/wiki/Long_Range_Reconnaissance_Patrol_(Sri_Lanka)" title="Long Range Reconnaissance Patrol (Sri Lanka)">Long Range Reconnaissance Patrol (Sri Lanka)</a> (LRRP).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Abrogation_of_ceasefire_agreement">Abrogation of ceasefire agreement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Abrogation of ceasefire agreement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Defense secretary <a href="/wiki/Gotabhaya_Rajapaksa" title="Gotabhaya Rajapaksa">Gotabhaya Rajapaksa</a> urged the government to abandon the ceasefire agreement in December 2007,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Daily_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-Daily-167">[167]</a></sup> and on 2 January 2008, the Sri Lankan government officially did so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-afp_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-afp-168">[168]</a></sup> Between February 2002 to May 2007, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Monitoring_Mission" title="Sri Lanka Monitoring Mission">Sri Lanka Monitoring Mission</a> had documented 3,830 ceasefire violations by the LTTE versus 351 by the security forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rep_4-9"><a href="#cite_note-rep-4">[4]</a></sup> From May 2007, the SLMM ceased making determinations on ceasefire violations. Thus the government stated there was no need for a ceasefire any more. Several donor countries expressed their disappointment at the Sri Lankan government's withdrawal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ministry_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ministry-169">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foreign_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-Foreign-170">[170]</a></sup> The LTTE formally responded that since the government had unilaterally withdrawn from the ceasefire agreement without any justification and that they were prepared to continue to honour the agreement, the international community ought to immediately remove the bans it had placed on the LTTE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-171">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cfa_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-cfa-172">[172]</a></sup></p>
<p>The government then attempted to open a third front along the <a href="/wiki/Muhamalai_Forward_Defence_Line" title="Muhamalai Forward Defence Line">Muhamalai Forward Defence Line</a>. After an initial setback on 23 April,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apr2308_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-apr2308-173">[173]</a></sup> the Sri Lankan Army advanced rapidly, capturing the town of Adampan on 9 May,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-ma-05.2F09.2F08_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-ma-05.2F09.2F08-174">[174]</a></sup> Mannar "Rice Bowl" which consists of the island's most fertile paddy fields on 30 June,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloomb_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-bloomb-175">[175]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vidattaltivu" title="Vidattaltivu">Vidattaltivu</a> on 16 July,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-ma-16_July_2008_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-ma-16_July_2008-176">[176]</a></sup> and Iluppaikkadavai on 20 July.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-ma-20_July_2008_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-ma-20_July_2008-177">[177]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 21 July 2008, the LTTE announced that it would be declaring a unilateral ceasefire from 28 July to 4 August, to coincide with the 15th summit of the heads of state of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SAARC" title="SAARC">SAARC</a> to be held in Colombo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dm_22_July_2008_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-dm_22_July_2008-178">[178]</a></sup> However, the government of Sri Lanka dismissed the LTTE's offer as needless and treacherous.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-ma-25_July_2008_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-ma-25_July_2008-179">[179]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Significant_military_gains_by_the_government">Significant military gains by the government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Significant military gains by the government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 2 August 2008, Vellankulam town, the LTTE's last stronghold in <a href="/wiki/Mannar_District" title="Mannar District">Mannar District</a>, fell to the advancing SLA troops, completing the eight-month effort to recapture the district.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-ma-08.2F02.2F08_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-ma-08.2F02.2F08-180">[180]</a></sup> The Army followed this up by taking control of <a href="/wiki/Mallavi" title="Mallavi">Mallavi</a> on 2 September, following weeks of heavy military confrontation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-ma-09.2F02.2F08_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-ma-09.2F02.2F08-181">[181]</a></sup> The LTTE countered with a surprise attack on the <a href="/wiki/Vavuniya" title="Vavuniya">Vavuniya</a> air base on 9 September, in which both sides claimed victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-va-9_September_2008_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-va-9_September_2008-182">[182]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-tn-9_September_2008_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-tn-9_September_2008-183">[183]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-bbc-09.2F10.2F08_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-bbc-09.2F10.2F08-184">[184]</a></sup></p>
<p>From Mannar, the Army had entered <a href="/wiki/Kilinochchi_District" title="Kilinochchi District">Kilinochchi District</a>, the last stronghold of the LTTE, at the end of July,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> with the intention of taking <a href="/wiki/Kilinochchi" title="Kilinochchi">Kilinochchi</a> before the end of the year. On 3 October 2008, a UN aid convoy managed to unload all its cargo in Kilinochchi District and described Kilinochchi town as having been nearly abandoned,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-bbc-10.2F03.2F08_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-bbc-10.2F03.2F08-186">[186]</a></sup> but the LTTE were able to kill retired Major General <a href="/wiki/Janaka_Perera" title="Janaka Perera">Janaka Perera</a> along with 26 other victims in a suicide blast on 6 October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-bbc-10.2F06.2F08_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-bbc-10.2F06.2F08-187">[187]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 17 October 2008, SLA troops cut off the <a href="/wiki/A32_highway_(Sri_Lanka)" title="A32 highway (Sri Lanka)">Mannar-Poonaryn A32 highway</a> north of Nachchikuda, the main remaining <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_Tiger" title="Sea Tiger">Sea Tiger</a> stronghold on the northwestern coast of the island, thus effectively encircling it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-ki-17_October_2008_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-ki-17_October_2008-188">[188]</a></sup> They began their assault on 28 October and captured it the next day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-ki-28_October_2008_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-ki-28_October_2008-189">[189]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-ki-29_October_2008_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-ki-29_October_2008-190">[190]</a></sup> After that the Army Task Force 1 continued their advance towards Pooneryn and captured Kiranchchi, Palavi, Veravil, Valaipadu and Devil's Point.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-ki-11_November_2008_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-ki-11_November_2008-191">[191]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-bbc-11_November_2008_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-bbc-11_November_2008-192">[192]</a></sup> On 15 November 2008, troops of the Army Task Force 1 entered the strategically important Tiger stronghold of <a href="/wiki/Pooneryn" title="Pooneryn">Pooneryn</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-bbc-15_November_2008_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-bbc-15_November_2008-193">[193]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-ki-15_November_2008_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-ki-15_November_2008-194">[194]</a></sup> Simultaneously, the newly created Army Task Force 3 was introduced into the area of <a href="/wiki/Maankulam_(Sri_Lanka)" title="Maankulam (Sri Lanka)">Mankulam</a> with the objective of engaging the LTTE cadres in a new battlefront towards the east of the <a href="/wiki/A9_highway_(Sri_Lanka)" title="A9 highway (Sri Lanka)">Jaffna–Kandy A9 highway</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-mu-11.2F03.2F08_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-mu-11.2F03.2F08-195">[195]</a></sup> SLA troops captured <a href="/wiki/Maankulam_(Sri_Lanka)" title="Maankulam (Sri Lanka)">Mankulam</a> and the surrounding area on 17 November 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-mu-17_November_2008_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-mu-17_November_2008-196">[196]</a></sup></p>
<p>Meanwhile, the situation of more than 200,000 civilians who had been displaced in the latest round of fighting was turning into a humanitarian disaster; however, due to a number of reasons including doubts regarding the sincerity of the LTTE's negotiations, neither Western governments nor India intervened to broker a new ceasefire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-bbc-10.2F17.2F08-2_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-bbc-10.2F17.2F08-2-197">[197]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fall_of_Kilinochchi_and_subsequent_events">Fall of Kilinochchi and subsequent events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Fall of Kilinochchi and subsequent events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kilinochchi_(2008%E2%80%932009)" title="Battle of Kilinochchi (2008–2009)">Battle of Kilinochchi (2008–2009)</a></div>
<p>The Sri Lankan Army began the attack on Kilinochchi on 23 November 2008. Troops were attacking rebels' defences from three directions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-bbc-24_November_2008_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-bbc-24_November_2008-198">[198]</a></sup> However, the LTTE offered a stiff resistance, and the prolonged attack resulted in heavy casualties on both sides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-bbc-17_December_2008_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-bbc-17_December_2008-199">[199]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tractors._Jan_2009_displacement_in_the_Vanni.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="1024" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Tractors._Jan_2009_displacement_in_the_Vanni.jpg/260px-Tractors._Jan_2009_displacement_in_the_Vanni.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Tractors._Jan_2009_displacement_in_the_Vanni.jpg/390px-Tractors._Jan_2009_displacement_in_the_Vanni.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Tractors._Jan_2009_displacement_in_the_Vanni.jpg/520px-Tractors._Jan_2009_displacement_in_the_Vanni.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tractors._Jan_2009_displacement_in_the_Vanni.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Civilians being displaced as a result of the Sri Lanka Army's military offensive. January 2009.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Not until 1 January 2009 were SLA troops able to capture <a href="/wiki/Paranthan" title="Paranthan">Paranthan</a>, located to the north of Kilinochchi along the A-9 route. This isolated the southern periphery of the <a href="/wiki/Elephant_Pass" title="Elephant Pass">Elephant Pass</a> LTTE foothold and also exposed the LTTE's main fortification at Kilinochchi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-ki-1_January_2009_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-ki-1_January_2009-200">[200]</a></sup> This made the capture of Kilinochchi, which the rebels had used for over a decade as their de facto administrative capital, far simpler, and they were able to accomplish this on 2 January. The loss of Killinochchi caused a substantial dent in the LTTE's image as a capable, ruthless terrorist group,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> and observers forecast the LTTE was likely to collapse before long under unbearable military pressure on multiple fronts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Tigers quickly abandoned their positions on the Jaffna peninsula to make a last stand in the jungles of <a href="/wiki/Mullaitivu" title="Mullaitivu">Mullaitivu</a>, their last main base.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-bbc-01.2F08.2F09_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-bbc-01.2F08.2F09-203">[203]</a></sup> The entire Jaffna peninsula was captured by the Sri Lanka Army by 14 January 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> However, they were unable to hold out for long, and on 25 January, SLA troops captured Mullaitivu.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-bbc-25_January_2009_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-bbc-25_January_2009-205">[205]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes_2009.2F01.2F26_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes_2009.2F01.2F26-206">[206]</a></sup> The last Sea Tiger base in Chalai was next to fall on 5 February, reducing the territory under rebel control to less than some 200 km<sup>2</sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-mu-02.2F05.2F09_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-mu-02.2F05.2F09-207">[207]</a></sup></p>
<p>This stage of the war was marked by increased brutality against civilians and rapidly mounting civilian casualties. On 19 February 2009, <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> issued a report accusing the Sri Lankan army of "slaughtering" the civilians during indiscriminate artillery attacks (including repeated shelling of hospitals) and calling on the Sri Lankan government to end its policy of "detaining displaced persons" in military-controlled internment camps. Human Rights Watch also urged the Tamil Tigers to permit trapped civilians to leave the war zone and to "stop shooting at those who try to flee".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hrw-19_February_2008_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-hrw-19_February_2008-208">[208]</a></sup> The UN was also concerned over the condition of internally displaced persons and estimated that some 200,000 people were being squeezed into a narrow 14 square kilometre patch of land on the coast in Vanni, which the government had declared the 'no-fire zone'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un-27_February_2008_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-un-27_February_2008-209">[209]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 20 February 2009, two LTTE planes on <a href="/wiki/2009_suicide_air_raid_on_Colombo" title="2009 suicide air raid on Colombo">a suicide mission</a> carried out a <a href="/wiki/Kamikaze" title="Kamikaze">kamikaze</a> style air attack on the Sri Lankan capital <a href="/wiki/Colombo" title="Colombo">Colombo</a>, killing 2 and wounding 45, but both planes were shot down by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_Air_Force" title="Sri Lankan Air Force">Sri Lankan Air Force</a> before they could damage the intended targets which were the Army Headquarters and the main Air Force base.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-australian-nottamed_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-australian-nottamed-210">[210]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> By late March, the Tamil Tigers controlled only one square kilometre outside the no-fire zone, down from about 15,000 km<sup>2</sup> a mere three years ago. Political pressure was placed on President Rajapaksa to find a political solution to the conflict and he called for a meeting with <a href="/wiki/Tamil_National_Alliance" title="Tamil National Alliance">Tamil National Alliance</a>, but they refused until the government resolved the humanitarian crisis faced by civilians trapped in the fighting.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Aanandapuram" title="Battle of Aanandapuram">Battle of Aanandapuram</a>, which was described by military analyst/journalist <a href="/wiki/D._B._S._Jeyaraj" title="D. B. S. Jeyaraj">D. B. S. Jeyaraj</a> as the "defining moment" of the 3 decade war, was fought on 5 April. This battle saw the demise of most of the battle-hardened ground commanders of the LTTE, including Velayuthapillai Baheerathakumar <i>alias</i> Theepan, the overall commander of the LTTE northern front fighting formations. SLA soldiers numbering more than 50,000 from 5 divisions participated in the battle encircling the LTTE cadres inside a small littoral strip of territory located between the <a href="/wiki/A35_highway_(Sri_Lanka)" title="A35 highway (Sri Lanka)">Paranthan-Mullaitivu A35 highway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nanthi_Lagoon" title="Nanthi Lagoon">Nanthikadal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chalai_Lagoon" title="Chalai Lagoon">Chalai Lagoons</a> on one side and the Indian ocean on the other. Rebel casualties amounted to 625.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fighting_in_the_.27No-Fire_Zone.27">Fighting in the 'No-Fire Zone'</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Fighting in the 'No-Fire Zone'">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>SLA troops were able to push the Tamil Tigers into the no-fire zone set up for civilians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-mu-04.2F05.2F09_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-mu-04.2F05.2F09-213">[213]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> The LTTE then built a 3-kilometre (2 mi) long <a href="/wiki/Bunding" title="Bunding">bund</a> in the no-fire zone, trapping over 30,000 civilians, but the SLA was able to destroy this.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-mu-20_April_2009_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-mu-20_April_2009-215">[215]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 21 April, Sri Lankan troops launched an assault, targeting LTTE leader, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vellupillai_Prabhakaran" title="Vellupillai Prabhakaran">Vellupillai Prabhakaran</a>. At the same time, a mass Tamil exodus from the 'no-fire zone' was underway.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> The next day, two senior LTTE members (LTTE media co-ordinator Velayuthan Thayanithi, <i>alias</i> Daya Master, and a top interpreter Kumar Pancharathnam, <i>alias</i> George)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> surrendered to the advancing Sri Lankan army. This came as "a rude shock" and a major setback for the rebel leadership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup> When asked why they had surrendered, both men stressed that rebels were shooting at the civilians and preventing them from escaping from the 'no-fire zone' to safety in government-controlled areas. They also alleged that the LTTE were still abducting and conscripting children as young as 14 years old, and would fire at anyone who tried to resist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 25 April, the area under the LTTE was reduced to 10 km<sup>2</sup>. While the Tamil exodus from the 'no-fire zone' continued, the UN estimated that around 6,500 civilians may have been killed and another 14,000 wounded between January 2009 and April 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> The BBC reported that the land recaptured by the army from the rebels was totally depopulated and utterly devastated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup></p>
<p>As fighting continued, a group of independent United Nations experts called on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Council" title="Human Rights Council">Human Rights Council</a> to urgently set up an international inquiry to address the "critical" situation in Sri Lanka amid fighting between the Army and Tamil rebels. According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Office_for_the_Coordination_of_Humanitarian_Affairs" title="UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs">UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OCHA" title="OCHA">OCHA</a>), over 196,000 people fled the conflict zone, a shrinking pocket of land on the north-east coastline, where clashes continued between government troops and the LTTE, while at least 50,000 people were still trapped there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> A UN spokesman in Colombo, Gordon Weiss, said more than 100 children died during the "large-scale killing of civilians" and described the situation in northern Sri Lanka as a "bloodbath".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> UN Secretary-General <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a> said he was appalled at the killing of hundreds of Sri Lankan civilians caught in the middle of hostilities between the army and separatist Tamil rebels over the weekend. He voiced deep concern over the continued use of heavy weapons in the conflict zone, but also stressed that the "reckless disrespect shown by the LTTE for the safety of civilians has led to thousands of people remaining trapped in the area".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 16 May 2009, Sri Lankan troops broke through LTTE defences and captured the last section of coastline held by Tamil Tiger rebels. The army reported it was set to "clear" remaining rebel-held land within days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-mu-16_May_2009_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-mu-16_May_2009-230">[230]</a></sup> Later the military claimed, allegedly citing intercepted LTTE communication, that rebels were preparing for a <a href="/wiki/Mass_suicide" title="Mass suicide">mass suicide</a> after being effectively cut off from escape routes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mod-nfz-16_May_2009_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-mod-nfz-16_May_2009-231">[231]</a></sup> Some rebels were reported to have blown themselves up.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="End_of_the_war">End of the war</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: End of the war">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="16_May:_Sri_Lanka_declares_victory">16 May: Sri Lanka declares victory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: 16 May: Sri Lanka declares victory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Addressing the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_Eleven" title="Group of Eleven">G11</a> summit in Jordan, <a href="/wiki/President_of_Sri_Lanka" title="President of Sri Lanka">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Mahinda_Rajapaksa" title="Mahinda Rajapaksa">Mahinda Rajapaksa</a> stated "my government, with the total commitment of our armed forces, has in an unprecedented humanitarian operation finally defeated the LTTE militarily".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-voas_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-voas-16">[16]</a></sup> Sri Lankan <a href="/wiki/Commander_of_the_Army_(Sri_Lanka)" title="Commander of the Army (Sri Lanka)">Commander of the Army</a> <a href="/wiki/Sarath_Fonseka" title="Sarath Fonseka">Sarath Fonseka</a> also declared victory over LTTE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> Sri Lankan troops raced to clear the last LTTE pockets of resistance. As the last LTTE strongpoints crumbled, Sri Lankan troops killed 70 rebels attempting to escape by boat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tonline_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-tonline-234">[234]</a></sup> The whereabouts of LTTE leader <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vellupillai_Prabhakaran" title="Vellupillai Prabhakaran">Vellupillai Prabhakaran</a> and other major rebel leaders were not certain.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="17_May:_Tigers_admit_defeat">17 May: Tigers admit defeat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: 17 May: Tigers admit defeat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The LTTE finally admitted defeat on 17 May 2009, with the rebels' chief of international relations, <a href="/wiki/Selvarasa_Pathmanathan" title="Selvarasa Pathmanathan">Selvarasa Pathmanathan</a>, stating on the website that "This battle has reached its bitter end ... We have decided to silence our guns. Our only regrets are for the lives lost and that we could not hold out for longer".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tonline1_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-tonline1-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-correspondentscivil_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-correspondentscivil-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="18_May:_First_claim_of_Prabhakaran.27s_death">18 May: First claim of Prabhakaran's death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: 18 May: First claim of Prabhakaran's death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Sri Lankan armed forces claimed that the leader of the LTTE, <a href="/wiki/Velupillai_Prabhakaran" title="Velupillai Prabhakaran">Velupillai Prabhakaran</a>, was killed in the morning of 18 May 2009 while he was trying to flee the conflict zone in an ambulance. The announcement on state television came shortly after the military said it had surrounded Prabhakaran in a tiny patch of jungle in the north-east. <i>The Daily Telegraph</i> wrote that, according to Sri Lankan TV, Prabhakaran was "... killed in a rocket-propelled grenade attack as he tried to escape the war zone in an Ambulance with his closest aides. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonel_Soosai" title="Colonel Soosai">Colonel Soosai</a>, the leader of his "<a href="/wiki/Sea_Tigers" title="Sea Tigers">Sea Tigers</a>" navy, and <a href="/wiki/Pottu_Amman_(Tamil_militant)" title="Pottu Amman (Tamil militant)">Pottu Amman</a>, his intelligence chief were also killed in the attack."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup></p>
<p>The head of the Sri Lankan army, General <a href="/wiki/Sarath_Fonseka" title="Sarath Fonseka">Sarath Fonseka</a>, said the military had defeated the rebels and "liberated the entire country". Military spokesman <a href="/wiki/Brigadier" title="Brigadier">Brigadier</a> <a href="/wiki/Udaya_Nanayakkara" title="Udaya Nanayakkara">Udaya Nanayakkara</a> stated 250 Tamil Tigers, who were hiding and fighting from within the no fire zone,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup> were killed overnight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19_May:_President_addresses_the_Parliament_and_Prabhakaran_is_dead">19 May: President addresses the Parliament and Prabhakaran is dead</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: 19 May: President addresses the Parliament and Prabhakaran is dead">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>At 9:00 am on 19 May 2009 <a href="/wiki/President_of_Sri_Lanka" title="President of Sri Lanka">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Mahinda_Rajapaksa" title="Mahinda Rajapaksa">Mahinda Rajapaksa</a> delivered a victory address to the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Parliament of Sri Lanka">Parliament</a> and declared that Sri Lanka is liberated from terrorism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup> Around 9:30 am troops attached to Task Force VIII of <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Army" title="Sri Lanka Army">Sri Lanka Army</a>, reported to its commander, <a href="/wiki/Colonel" title="Colonel">Colonel</a> G.V. Ravipriya that a body similar to Velupillai Prabhakaran has been found among the mangroves in Nandikadal lagoon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lankaw_240-0"><a href="#cite_note-lankaw-240">[240]</a></sup> It was identified by the officer. At 12:15 pm Army Commander <a href="/wiki/Sarath_Fonseka" title="Sarath Fonseka">Sarath Fonseka</a> officially announced Prabhakaran's death, through the State television <a href="/wiki/Independent_Television_Network" title="Independent Television Network">ITN</a>. At around 1:00 pm his body was shown in <a href="/wiki/Swarnavahini" title="Swarnavahini">Swarnavahini</a> for the first time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup> Prabakaran's identity was confirmed by <a href="/wiki/Vinayagamoorthy_Muralitharan" title="Vinayagamoorthy Muralitharan">Karuna Amman</a>, his former confidant, and through DNA testing against his son's genetic material who had been killed earlier by the Sri Lanka Military.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DNA_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-DNA-242">[242]</a></sup> However, LTTE Chief of international relations, <a href="/wiki/Selvarasa_Pathmanathan" title="Selvarasa Pathmanathan">Selvarasa Pathmanathan</a> on the same day claimed that "Our beloved leader is alive and safe."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pathman_243-0"><a href="#cite_note-pathman-243">[243]</a></sup> On 24 May 2009, he admitted the death of Prabhakaran, retracting the previous statement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-expr_244-0"><a href="#cite_note-expr-244">[244]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reaction">Reaction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Reaction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Reactions_to_the_end_of_the_Sri_Lankan_Civil_War" title="Reactions to the end of the Sri Lankan Civil War">Reactions to the end of the Sri Lankan Civil War</a></div>
<p>The general public of Sri Lanka took to streets to celebrate the end of the decades long war. Streets were filled with joyous scenes of jubilation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-celeb_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-celeb-245">[245]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-celeb2_246-0"><a href="#cite_note-celeb2-246">[246]</a></sup> Opposition leader Ranil Wickremasinghe, through a telephone call, congratulated President Rajapaksa and the state security forces for their victory over the LTTE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup> Religious leaders too hailed the end of the bloodshed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup> International response to the end of the fighting was also positive and welcoming, while some countries expressed concern over the civilian casualties and the humanitarian impact. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretary_General" title="United Nations Secretary General">United Nations Secretary General</a> <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a> said, "I am relieved by the conclusion of the military operation, but I am deeply troubled by the loss of so many civilian lives. The task now facing the people of Sri Lanka is immense and requires all hands. It is most important that every effort be undertaken to begin a process of healing and national reconciliation".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a> magazine named the end of the Sri Lankan Civil War as one of the top 10 news stories of 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Combat_after_18_May_2009">Combat after 18 May 2009</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Combat after 18 May 2009">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>19 May 2009 – 3 LTTE cadre killed by the Sri Lankan Army at Kachikudichchiaru, <a href="/wiki/Ampara" title="Ampara">Ampara</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-detailed1_251-0"><a href="#cite_note-detailed1-251">[251]</a></sup></li>
<li>20 May 2009 – 5 LTTE cadre killed by the Sri Lankan Army near Periyapillumalai area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-detailed1_251-1"><a href="#cite_note-detailed1-251">[251]</a></sup></li>
<li>21 May 2009 – 10 LTTE cadre killed by the Sri Lankan Army in the Kadawana jungle area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup></li>
<li>27 May 2009 – 11 LTTE cadre killed by the Sri Lankan Army at Kalavanchchikudi in the Batticaloa area. Five T-56 assault rifles, twenty claymore mines (15 kg each), two hand grenades, three anti-personnel mines and medical items were reported recovered by military sources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup></li>
<li>5 June 2009 – Special Task Force (STF) personnel while conducting search and clear operation in Darampalawa area in <a href="/wiki/Ampara" title="Ampara">Ampara</a> confronted a group of LTTE cadre and recovered two bodies along with numerous military items.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup></li>
<li>5 August 2009 – <a href="/wiki/Selvarasa_Pathmanathan" title="Selvarasa Pathmanathan">Selvarasa Pathmanathan</a>, the new leader of LTTE was arrested by a Sri Lankan military intelligence unit, with the collaboration of local authorities, in the <a href="/wiki/Tune_Hotels#Malaysia" title="Tune Hotels">Tune Hotel</a>, Downtown <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a>, Malaysia and brought back to Sri Lanka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cost_of_war">Cost of war</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Cost of war">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shelter_from_tarp_and_sticks.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Shelter_from_tarp_and_sticks.jpg/220px-Shelter_from_tarp_and_sticks.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Shelter_from_tarp_and_sticks.jpg/330px-Shelter_from_tarp_and_sticks.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Shelter_from_tarp_and_sticks.jpg/440px-Shelter_from_tarp_and_sticks.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shelter_from_tarp_and_sticks.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Shelter built from tarp and sticks. Pictured are displaced persons from the civil war in Sri Lanka</div>
