<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Casualties">Casualties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Casualties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Casualties_of_the_Sri_Lankan_Civil_War" title="Casualties of the Sri Lankan Civil War">Casualties of the Sri Lankan Civil War</a></div>
<p>The Sri Lankan civil war was very costly in terms of human lives lost. Estimates vary depending on the years included in the conflict, for example the <a href="/wiki/Uppsala_Conflict_Data_Program" title="Uppsala Conflict Data Program">Uppsala Conflict Data Program</a> reported that between 1990 and 2009 between 59,193–75,601<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup> people were killed in organized armed conflict while the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> estimated that between 80,000–100,000 people were killed from 1982 to 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABC200509_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-ABC200509-14">[14]</a></sup> The deaths include at least 27,639 LTTE fighters, 23,790 Sri Lankan soldiers and policemen, 1,155 Indian soldiers, and tens of thousands of civilians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lessons_Learnt_and_Reconciliation_Commission" title="Lessons Learnt and Reconciliation Commission">Lessons Learnt and Reconciliation Commission</a> concluded that from August 2006 (recapture of the Mavil Aru reservoir) to 18 May 2009 (the formal declaration of the cessation of hostilities), 5,556 Sri Lankan soldiers were killed, 28,414 were wounded and 169 were <a href="/wiki/Missing_in_action" title="Missing in action">missing in action</a>. During this period, LTTE lost 22,247 cadres of which 11,812 had been identified by name.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-llrc_258-0"><a href="#cite_note-llrc-258">[258]</a></sup></p>
<p>The number of civilian casualties has been subject to intense debate. While the loss of civilian lives has been prevalent during the entire conflict, the final five months saw the heaviest attrition rate. United Nations, based on credible witness evidence from aid agencies as well civilians evacuated from the <i>Safe Zone</i> by sea, estimated that 6,500 civilians were killed and another 14,000 injured between mid-January 2009 (when the <i>Safe Zone</i> was first declared) and mid-April 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TG240409_259-0"><a href="#cite_note-TG240409-259">[259]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC270409_260-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC270409-260">[260]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i>, the British daily, estimates the death toll for the final four months of the war (from mid-January to mid-May) to be 20,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most of the details pertaining to the civilian casualties were reported by four doctors who worked in the no-fire zone. In a joint press conference after the war in July 2009 while still in <a href="/wiki/Criminal_Investigation_Department_(Sri_Lanka)" title="Criminal Investigation Department (Sri Lanka)">CID</a> custody, they recanted their initial reports, stating that the casualty figures were exaggerated and were handed to them by the LTTE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc080709_263-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc080709-263">[263]</a></sup> However, a <a href="/wiki/United_States_diplomatic_cables_leak" title="United States diplomatic cables leak">leaked US diplomatic cable</a> contains dispatches stating that the doctors upon their release in August 2009 are to have stated to US embassy personnel that they were heavily coached for the press conference and that they had not lied when giving their original statements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[264]</a></sup></p>
<p>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_State_Department" title="US State Department">US State Department</a> report has suggested that the actual casualty figures were probably much higher than the UN estimates and that significant numbers of casualties were not recorded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_265-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-265">[265]</a></sup> Gordon Weiss, a former UN official has claimed that up to 40,000 civilians may have been killed in the final stages of the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup> U.N Secretary General's experts panel report had said that as many as 40,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tamil_people" title="Tamil people">Tamil</a> civilians could have been killed in the final phases of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_civil_war" title="Sri Lankan civil war">Sri Lankan civil war</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup> On the contrary, <a href="/wiki/Rajiva_Wijesinha" title="Rajiva Wijesinha">Rajiva Wijesinha</a> the permanent secretary to the Sri Lanka's Ministry of Disaster Management and Human Rights, in June 2009 said that altogether 3,000 to 5,000 civilians may have been killed during the period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup> In November 2011, a Sri Lankan international terrorism expert, Rohan Gunaratna, estimated the number of civilian casualties to be 1,400 (1200 killed by army cross-fire and 200 by LTTE). His estimate is in part based on information obtained from captured LTTE cadres to which he had been granted access and from coroners working in and around the no-fire zone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270"><a href="#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2012, the Sri Lankan government released an official estimate of civilian deaths in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Province,_Sri_Lanka" title="Northern Province, Sri Lanka">Northern Province</a>, concluding that 8,649 people have died due to extraordinary circumstances (reasons other than ageing, diseases, natural disasters etc.), in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eve2011_271-0"><a href="#cite_note-eve2011-271">[271]</a></sup> It also listed 2,635 people as untraceable. However the report did not differentiate civilians from the slain LTTE cadres.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_cost">Economic cost</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Economic cost">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The total economic cost of the 26-year war is estimated at US$200 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup> This is approximately 5 times the GDP of Sri Lanka in 2009. Sri Lanka had spent US$5.5 billion only on Eelam War IV, which saw the end of LTTE. The government had spent US$2.25 billion to develop the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Province,_Sri_Lanka" title="Northern Province, Sri Lanka">Northern Province</a> under the "Uthuru Wasanthaya" program after the end of war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-obsy_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-obsy-13">[13]</a></sup> Measuring the opportunity cost of war, a report by <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Foresight_Group" title="Strategic Foresight Group">Strategic Foresight Group</a> states that Foreign Direct Investment (FDI) remained stagnant during periods of civil war and that net FDI increased during periods of ceasefire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A_political_solution">A political solution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: A political solution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After the complete military defeat of the LTTE, President Mahinda Rajapaksa announced that the government is committed to a political solution, and for this purpose action would be taken based on the 13th Amendment to the Constitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup> Pro-LTTE political party <a href="/wiki/Tamil_National_Alliance" title="Tamil National Alliance">Tamil National Alliance</a> (TNA), also the largest political group representing Sri Lankan Tamil community, dropped its demand for a <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Eelam" title="Tamil Eelam">separate state</a>, in favour of a <a href="/wiki/Federalism" title="Federalism">federal</a> solution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc1_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbc1-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardn_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-guardn-30">[30]</a></sup> There are ongoing bilateral talks between President Rajapaksa's <a href="/wiki/United_People%27s_Freedom_Alliance" title="United People's Freedom Alliance">UPFA</a> government and the TNA, on a viable political solution and devolution of power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, in an interview to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Headlines_Today" title="Headlines Today">Headlines Today</a>, television channel from India, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gotabaya_Rajapaksa" title="Gotabaya Rajapaksa">Gotabaya Rajapaksa</a>, Defence Secretary of Sri Lanka and brother of President <a href="/wiki/Mahinda_Rajapaksa" title="Mahinda Rajapaksa">Mahinda Rajapaksa</a> binned "the political solution talk", asserting, among other things, that it was "simply irrelevant" because "we have ended this terrorism" in Sri Lanka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277">[277]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lessons_Learnt_and_Reconciliation_Commission">Lessons Learnt and Reconciliation Commission</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Lessons Learnt and Reconciliation Commission">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lessons_Learnt_and_Reconciliation_Commission" title="Lessons Learnt and Reconciliation Commission">Lessons Learnt and Reconciliation Commission</a></div>
<p>Following the end of the war in May 2009, amid mounting international pressure for an inquiry into the final stages of the war, President Rajapaksa appointed the Lessons Learnt and Reconciliation Commission (LLRC) to look back at the Sri Lankan Civil War, and to provide recommendations for an era of healing and peace building. The commission concluded that the <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Armed_Forces" title="Sri Lanka Armed Forces">Sri Lankan military</a> didn't deliberately target civilians in the No Fire Zones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBS161211_279-0"><a href="#cite_note-CBS161211-279">[279]</a></sup> The commission acknowledged that hospitals had been shelled, resulting "considerable civilian casualties", but it did not say who was responsible for the shelling. The commission blamed Sinhalese and Tamil politicians for causing the civil war: the Sinhalese politicians failed to offer a solution acceptable to the Tamil people and the Tamil politicians fanned <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_Tamil_militant_groups" title="Sri Lankan Tamil militant groups">militant separatism</a>. However the commission has been heavily criticised by human rights groups and UN Secretary-General's Panel of Experts on Accountability due its limited mandate, alleged lack of independence and its failure to meet minimum international standards or offer protection to witnesses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-C4161211_280-0"><a href="#cite_note-C4161211-280">[280]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Humanitarian_Impact">Humanitarian Impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Humanitarian Impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_IDP_camps" title="Sri Lankan IDP camps">Sri Lankan IDP camps</a></div>
<p>Towards the end of the war, as Sri Lankan government forces advanced deeper into Tamil Tiger controlled areas, international concern grew for the fate of the 350,000 civilians trapped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup> On 21 January 2009, the Sri Lankan military declared a 32 square kilometres (12.4 mi) <i>Safe Zone</i> located northwest of Puthukkudiviruppu, between the A35 Highway and the Chalai Lagoon. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_Air_Force" title="Sri Lankan Air Force">Sri Lankan Air Force</a> aircraft dropped leaflets urging civilians to relocate to the safe zone and wait until the army could move them into safer locations. The Sri Lankan military promised not to fire into the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282"><a href="#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup> However, only small numbers of civilians actually crossed into the Safe Zone, and the Sri Lankan government, the United Nations, and human rights organisations accused the LTTE of preventing civilians from leaving. The fighting eventually caused civilians to flee the safe zone to a narrow strip of land between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanthi_Kadal" title="Nanthi Kadal">Nanthi Kadal</a> and the Indian Ocean. The Sri Lankan military declared a new 10-square-kilometre (3.9 sq mi) Safe Zone northwest of <a href="/wiki/Mullaitivu" title="Mullaitivu">Mullaitivu</a> on 12 February. Over the next three months, the Sri Lankan military repeatedly attacked the Safe Zone with aircraft and artillery to destroy the last remnants of the Tamil Tigers trapped there. The Sri Lankan government claimed that it was trying to hit Tamil Tiger positions, and claimed that these raids started on 15 February and ended on 19 April, the day before the Army breached Tamil Tiger defences, and civilians started to pour out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-283"><a href="#cite_note-283">[283]</a></sup> However, these attacks caused heavy damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284"><a href="#cite_note-284">[284]</a></sup> Thousands of civilians were killed or injured, and the Tamil Tigers reportedly held many as human shields.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285"><a href="#cite_note-285">[285]</a></sup></p>
<p>The final stages of the war created 300,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_persons" title="Internally displaced persons">internally displaced persons</a> (IDPs) who were transferred to camps in <a href="/wiki/Vavuniya_District" title="Vavuniya District">Vavuniya District</a> and detained there against their will.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286"><a href="#cite_note-286">[286]</a></sup> The camps were surrounded by barbed wire. This, together with the conditions inside the camps, attracted much criticism from inside and outside Sri Lanka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-287"><a href="#cite_note-287">[287]</a></sup> After the end of the civil war President Rajapaksa gave assurances to foreign diplomats that the bulk of the IDPs would be resettled in accordance with the 180-day plan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288">[288]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289"><a href="#cite_note-289">[289]</a></sup> By January 2012, almost all the IDPs had been resettled, except 6,554 from the <a href="/wiki/Divisional_Secretariats_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Divisional Secretariats of Sri Lanka">Divisional Secretariats</a> of Mullaitivu district, where the de-mining work was yet to be finished.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290"><a href="#cite_note-290">[290]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since 1983, the civil war caused mass outflow of Tamil civilians from Sri Lanka to South India. After the end of the war, nearly 5,000 of them returned to the country. As of July 2012, 68,152 Sri Lankans were living in South India as refugees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291"><a href="#cite_note-291">[291]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Detainees">Detainees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Detainees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The continuous defeats of the LTTE had made its cadres abandon the outfit in large numbers. With the end of the hostilities, 11,664 LTTE members, including over 500 child soldiers surrendered to the Sri Lankan military. Among them were 1,601 females. Government took action to rehabilitate these cadres under a "National Action Plan for the Re-integration of Ex-combatants". They were divided into 3 categories; hardcore, non-combatants, and those who were forcefully recruited (including child soldiers). 24 rehabilitation centres were set up in Jaffna, Batticaloa and Vavuniya. Among the apprehended cadres, there had been about 700 hardcore members. Some of these cadres were integrated into State Intelligence Services to tackle the internal and external networks of LTTE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-obshgd_292-0"><a href="#cite_note-obshgd-292">[292]</a></sup> By January 2012, government had released more than 11,000 cadres, and only 4 rehabilitation centres and 550 detainees remained.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-detn_293-0"><a href="#cite_note-detn-293">[293]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Land_mines">Land mines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Land mines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The end of the war left past conflict zones of 2,061sq.km heavily contaminated with approximately 1.6 million land mines. By January 2012, deminers employed by the Sri Lankan army and 8 foreign funded agencies had cleared 1,934sq.km leaving about 127sq.km yet to be cleared.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-294"><a href="#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the end of the war, more than 5,000 Tamil youths have been gathering at selected police stations in Eastern Province to join the police force as the government has called for interviews. The Sri Lankan government had planned to recruit 2,000 new police officers to the department, especially for the services in the northern region of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-295"><a href="#cite_note-295">[295]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Protests">Protests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Protests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2009_Tamil_diaspora_protests" title="2009 Tamil diaspora protests">2009 Tamil diaspora protests</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tamil_protest_on_University_Avenue.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Tamil_protest_on_University_Avenue.jpg/250px-Tamil_protest_on_University_Avenue.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Tamil_protest_on_University_Avenue.jpg/375px-Tamil_protest_on_University_Avenue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Tamil_protest_on_University_Avenue.jpg/500px-Tamil_protest_on_University_Avenue.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tamil_protest_on_University_Avenue.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tamil_Canadian" title="Tamil Canadian">Canadian Tamils</a> block University Avenue, <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a> demonstrating against the Sri Lankan forces.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tamil_diaspora" title="Tamil diaspora">Tamil diaspora</a> communities around the world protested the civilian casualties in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Province,_Sri_Lanka" title="Northern Province, Sri Lanka">Northern Province, Sri Lanka</a> and the war in general. Active protests occurred in the major and/or capital cities of India,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aljazeera_296-0"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeera-296">[296]</a></sup> United Kingdom,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-297"><a href="#cite_note-297">[297]</a></sup> Canada,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-star1_298-0"><a href="#cite_note-star1-298">[298]</a></sup> Australia, Norway, Switzerland, Denmark, Germany and the United States. The collective objective of the protests was to persuade world national leaders to stop the civil war and bring a permanent ceasefire with an internationally coordinated diplomatic strategy.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="War_crimes_investigations">War crimes investigations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: War crimes investigations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In March 2014, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Commission" title="United Nations Human Rights Commission">United Nations Human Rights Commission</a> drafted a resolution on "Promoting reconciliation, accountability and human rights in Sri Lanka" and requested its High Commissioner Ms. <a href="/wiki/Navi_Pillay" title="Navi Pillay">Navi Pillay</a> to undertake a comprehensive investigation into alleged serious violations and human rights abuses that have taken place during the war. Subsequently, the Human Rights Commissioner directed the setting up of OHCHR Investigation in Sri Lanka (OISL).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ohchr_299-0"><a href="#cite_note-ohchr-299">[299]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Sri Lankan state which is accused of perpetuating <a href="/wiki/War_crime" title="War crime">war crimes</a>, has reportedly refused to cooperate with the inquiry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slg1_300-0"><a href="#cite_note-slg1-300">[300]</a></sup> In August 2014, the state rejected entry visas for investigating U.N. officials. Two months later, in October, Sri Lankan government banned all foreigners from visiting the former war zone altogether.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reuters_301-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-301">[301]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alleged_war_crimes">Alleged war crimes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Alleged war crimes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alleged_war_crimes_during_the_Sri_Lankan_Civil_War" title="Alleged war crimes during the Sri Lankan Civil War">Alleged war crimes during the Sri Lankan Civil War</a></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alleged_war_crimes_during_the_Sri_Lankan_Civil_War" title="Alleged war crimes during the Sri Lankan Civil War">Allegations of war crimes</a> have been made against the rebel <a href="/wiki/Liberation_Tigers_of_Tamil_Eelam" title="Liberation Tigers of Tamil Eelam">Liberation Tigers of Tamil Eelam</a> (Tamil Tigers) and the <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Armed_Forces" title="Sri Lanka Armed Forces">Sri Lankan military</a> with much attention given to the final months of the Civil War in 2009. The alleged war crimes include attacks on civilians and civilian buildings by both sides; executions of combatants and prisoners by both sides; enforced disappearances by the Sri Lankan military and paramilitary groups backed by them; acute shortages of food, medicine, and clean water for civilians trapped in the war zone; and child recruitment and attacks on targeting civilian including suicide bombings<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302"><a href="#cite_note-302">[302]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303"><a href="#cite_note-303">[303]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304"><a href="#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-305"><a href="#cite_note-305">[305]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news.bbc.co.uk_306-0"><a href="#cite_note-news.bbc.co.uk-306">[306]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-307"><a href="#cite_note-307">[307]</a></sup> and attacks on civilian aircraft by the Tamil Tigers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-308"><a href="#cite_note-308">[308]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-309"><a href="#cite_note-309">[309]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-310"><a href="#cite_note-310">[310]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-311"><a href="#cite_note-311">[311]</a></sup></p>
<p>Video footage showing uniformed men speaking Sinhalese and summarily executing eight bound and blindfolded men was broadcast in August 2009 by UK's Channel 4 in a program called "<a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka%27s_Killing_Fields" title="Sri Lanka's Killing Fields">Sri Lanka's Killing Fields</a>". This video was subsequently authenticated by the UN.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-312"><a href="#cite_note-312">[312]</a></sup> Reports commissioned by the Sri lankan government claim the UN authentication was biased and the video was fabricated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-313"><a href="#cite_note-313">[313]</a></sup></p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Report_of_the_Secretary-General%27s_Panel_of_Experts_on_Accountability_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Report of the Secretary-General's Panel of Experts on Accountability in Sri Lanka">panel of experts</a> appointed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Secretary-General" title="UN Secretary-General">UN Secretary-General</a> (UNSG) <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a> to advise him on the issue of <a href="/wiki/Accountability" title="Accountability">accountability</a> with regard to any alleged violations of <a href="/wiki/International_human_rights_law" title="International human rights law">international human rights</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_humanitarian_law" title="International humanitarian law">humanitarian law</a> during the final stages of the conflict in Sri Lanka found "credible allegations" which according to them, if proven, indicated that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_crimes" title="War crimes">war crimes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">crimes against humanity</a> were committed by the Sri Lankan military and the Tamil Tigers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Island160411_314-0"><a href="#cite_note-Island160411-314">[314]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TN160411_315-0"><a href="#cite_note-TN160411-315">[315]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DM160411_316-0"><a href="#cite_note-DM160411-316">[316]</a></sup> The panel has called on the UNSG to conduct an independent international inquiry into the alleged violations of <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-317"><a href="#cite_note-317">[317]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_government" title="Sri Lankan government">Sri Lankan government</a> has denied that its forces committed any war crimes and has strongly opposed any international investigation. It has condemned the UN report as "fundamentally flawed in many respects" and "based on patently biased material which is presented without any verification".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-318"><a href="#cite_note-318">[318]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Lessons_Learnt_and_Reconciliation_Commission" title="Lessons Learnt and Reconciliation Commission">Lessons Learnt and Reconciliation Commission</a>, a formal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commission_of_inquiry" title="Commission of inquiry">commission of inquiry</a> was appointed by the Sri Lankan President, to review the conflict from 1983 to 2009 and its report was tabled in the parliament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-319"><a href="#cite_note-319">[319]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 27 July 2012, Sri Lanka brought out a road map fixing time lines for investigating alleged war crimes by its army during the final stages of the war with the LTTE in 2009. The cabinet has approved the action plan for the implementation of the Lessons Learnt and Reconciliation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-320"><a href="#cite_note-320">[320]</a></sup></p>
<p>The UN High Commissioner for Human Rights said in September 2013 that there had been no comprehensive Sri Lankan effort to properly and independently investigate allegations of war crimes. The High Commissioner said she would recommend the Human Rights Council to set up its own probe if Sri Lanka does not show more "credible" progress by March 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-321"><a href="#cite_note-321">[321]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 27 March 2014 the United Nations Human Rights Council voted for a resolution paving the way for an inquiry into rights abuses at the end of Sri Lanka's civil war. The United States and the United Kingdom were among the countries which sponsored the resolution, which for the first time called for an international probe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-322"><a href="#cite_note-322">[322]</a></sup></p>
<p>The new government of <a href="/wiki/Maithripala_Sirisena" title="Maithripala Sirisena">President Maithripala Sirisena</a> has requested the international community for support on a domestic probe into war crimes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-323"><a href="#cite_note-323">[323]</a></sup> As of March 2015, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN" title="UN">UN</a> have expressed their support for this.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-324"><a href="#cite_note-324">[324]</a></sup> The Tamil National alliance has asked for an international investigation into the alleged human rights abuses during the Sri Lankan civil war and has refused a domestic probe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-325"><a href="#cite_note-325">[325]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-326"><a href="#cite_note-326">[326]</a></sup> A group of the TNA led by Wigneshwaran has asked for an investigation into the alleged genocide claims but the TNA as a whole was divided on the issue and MP Senathirajah said that the action was unauthorized by the party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-327"><a href="#cite_note-327">[327]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Tamil National Alliance has welcomed a domestic investigation with a hybrid court and <a href="/wiki/R._Sampanthan" title="R. Sampanthan">R. Sampanthan</a> praised several new initiatives from the new government and said "The government is adopting the correct position," and asked the government to honor to there commitments but some members such as <a href="/wiki/Ananthi_Sasitharan" title="Ananthi Sasitharan">Ananthi Sasitharan</a> had a less optimistic view.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-328"><a href="#cite_note-328">[328]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-329"><a href="#cite_note-329">[329]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-330"><a href="#cite_note-330">[330]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Allegations_of_Genocide">Allegations of Genocide</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Allegations of Genocide">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The first international voice to support the genocide against the Government of Sri Lanka under international law is raised by <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> and it has advocated and published the details in December 2009. Leading American expert in international law, Professor Francis A. Boyle hold an emergency meeting with U.N. Secretary-General Ban Ki-Moon to urge to stop Tamil genocide by providing the evidence of crimes against humanity, genocide against Tamils and the international community's failure to stop the slaughter of Tamil civilians in Sri Lanka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-331"><a href="#cite_note-331">[331]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-332"><a href="#cite_note-332">[332]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Permanent_Peoples%27_Tribunal" title="Permanent Peoples' Tribunal">Permanent People's Tribunal</a> on Sri Lankan held its sessions in Dublin, Ireland. There were four findings:</p>
<ol>
<li>That the Sri Lankan Government and its military are guilty of War Crimes;</li>
<li>That the Sri Lankan Government and its military are guilty of crimes against humanity;</li>
<li>That the charge of genocide requires further investigation;</li>
<li>That the international community, particularly the UK and USA, share responsibility for the breakdown of the peace process.(2)</li>
</ol>
<p>It also found that member states of the United Nations had not "complied with their moral obligation to seek justice for the violations of human rights committed during the last period of the war".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dublin-Tribunal-init_333-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dublin-Tribunal-init-333">[333]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 22 September 2010, the <a href="/wiki/UNROW_Human_Rights_Impact_Litigation_Clinic" title="UNROW Human Rights Impact Litigation Clinic">UNROW Human Rights Impact Litigation Clinic</a>, has advocated and litigated on behalf of victims of the armed conflict in <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNROW" title="UNROW">UNROW Human Rights Impact Litigation Clinic</a> released a report calling for the establishment of a new international tribunal to prosecute those most responsible for the crimes committed during the conflict. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNROW" title="UNROW">UNROW Human Rights Impact Litigation Clinic</a> also submitted evidence of human rights violations committed during the armed conflict to the United Nations Panel of Experts on Sri Lanka, which U.N. Secretary-General Ban Ki-Moon appointed in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LegalCaseOfTheTamil_334-0"><a href="#cite_note-LegalCaseOfTheTamil-334">[334]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November,03 2012, panel of 11 member International Experts, consisting of experts in genocide studies, former UN officials, experts in international law and renowned peace and human rights activists to be convened as Judges appointed by <a href="/wiki/Permanent_Peoples%27_Tribunal" title="Permanent Peoples' Tribunal">Permanent People's Tribunal</a> to investigate and examine reports submitted by many specialised working groups on the accusation of the crime of Genocide against the Government of Sri Lanka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dublin-Tribunal-init_333-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dublin-Tribunal-init-333">[333]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-335"><a href="#cite_note-335">[335]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 27 March 2013, Tamil Nadu State Assembly has passed resolution to called on the Indian Government to stop considering Sri Lanka as a 'friendly country' and impose economic sanctions, as well as calling for an international inquiry in "genocide and war crimes" against Sri Lankan Tamils.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-336"><a href="#cite_note-336">[336]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 10 December 2013, <a href="/wiki/Permanent_Peoples%27_Tribunal" title="Permanent Peoples' Tribunal">Permanent People's Tribunal</a> unanimously ruled Sri Lanka guilty of the crime of genocide against the Tamil people, while the US and UK were found to be guilty of complicity to this crime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-337"><a href="#cite_note-337">[337]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-338"><a href="#cite_note-338">[338]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-339"><a href="#cite_note-339">[339]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-340"><a href="#cite_note-340">[340]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January, 2015, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNROW" title="UNROW">UNROW Human Rights Impact Litigation Clinic</a> filed a paper on "The Legal Case of the Tamil Genocide" based on the evidence, nature and extent of the violence committed by Government Forces against Tamils.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LegalCaseOfTheTamil_334-1"><a href="#cite_note-LegalCaseOfTheTamil-334">[334]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 12 April 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Provincial_Council" title="Northern Provincial Council">Northern Provincial Council</a> of Sri Lanka <a href="/wiki/2015_Northern_Province_Council_resolution_on_genocide_of_Tamils" title="2015 Northern Province Council resolution on genocide of Tamils">passed a resolution</a> calling the UN to investigate the genocide and direct appropriate measures at the International Court of Justice stating that the Tamils had no faith in the domestic commission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tgnpc_341-0"><a href="#cite_note-tgnpc-341">[341]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nienpc_342-0"><a href="#cite_note-nienpc-342">[342]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wswsnpc_343-0"><a href="#cite_note-wswsnpc-343">[343]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lankan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li>Gamage, S.: <i>Ethnic Conflict, State Reform and Nation Building in Sri Lanka: Analysis of the Context and Suggestions for a Settlement</i>, in: Neelsen, John P. and Malik, Dipak: "Crises of State and Nation: South Asian States between Nation Building and Fragmentation", Manohar, New Delhi (forthcoming).</li>

<li>Johnson, Robert: <i>A Region in Turmoil</i>. Reaktion, New York and London 2005. (Covers Sri Lanka and its regional context.)</li>
<li>Narayan Swamy, M. R.: <i>Tigers of Lanka: from Boys to Guerrillas</i>. Konark Publishers; 3rd ed. 2002, <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/8122006310">ISBN 81-220-0631-0</a>.</li>
<li>Rajasinghan, K.T.: <i>Sri Lanka: The Untold Story</i>. 2001–2002. (Serialised in <i>Asia Times Online</i>).<a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20060515195046/http://www.atimes.com/atimes/others/untold_story.html" rel="nofollow">Sri Lanka: The Untold Story</a>.</li>
<li><i>War and Peace in Sri Lanka: With a Post-Accord Report From Jaffna</i>. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9552600014">ISBN 955-26-0001-4</a> /<a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9789552600012">ISBN 978-955-26-0001-2</a>, Institute of Fundamental Studies, Sri Lanka; 1 edition (1 October 1987), By <a href="/wiki/Rohan_Gunaratna" title="Rohan Gunaratna">Rohan Gunaratna</a>.</li>
<li><i>Indian intervention in Sri Lanka: The role of India's intelligence agencies</i>. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9559519905">ISBN 955-95199-0-5</a>/ <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9789559519904">ISBN 978-955-95199-0-4</a>, South Asian Network on Conflict Research (1993), By <a href="/wiki/Rohan_Gunaratna" title="Rohan Gunaratna">Rohan Gunaratna</a>.</li>
<li>Bansal, Alok, Mayilvaganan. M and Podder, Sukanya, <i>Sri Lanka: Search for Peace</i>. Manas Publications, New Delhi, 2007. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/8170493404">ISBN 81-7049-340-4</a></li>

<th class="navbox-group" scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;">Military</th>
